       <b>
        Trinidad and Tobago
       </b>
       (
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'t' in 'tie'">
            t
           </span>
           <span title="'r' in 'rye'">
            r
           </span>
           <span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">
            ɪ
           </span>
           <span title="'n' in 'nigh'">
            n
           </span>
           <span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">
            ɪ
           </span>
           <span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">
            ˌ
           </span>
           <span title="'d' in 'dye'">
            d
           </span>
           <span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">
            æ
           </span>
           <span title="'d' in 'dye'">
            d
           </span>
          </span>
          ...
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="'t' in 'tie'">
            t
           </span>
           <span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">
            ə
           </span>
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'b' in 'buy'">
            b
           </span>
           <span title="/eɪ/: 'a' in 'face'">
            eɪ
           </span>
           <span title="/ɡ/: 'g' in 'guy'">
            ɡ
           </span>
           <span title="/oʊ/: 'o' in 'code'">
            oʊ
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
        <small class="nowrap">
         (
         <span class="unicode haudio">
          <span class="fn">
           <span style="white-space:nowrap">
            <a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Trinidad_and_Tobago.ogg" title="About this sound">
             <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
            </a>
           </span>
           <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/de/En-us-Trinidad_and_Tobago.ogg" title="En-us-Trinidad and Tobago.ogg">
            listen
           </a>
          </span>
         </span>
         )
        </small>
       </span>
       ,
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="'t' in 'tie'">
            t
           </span>
           <span title="/oʊ/: 'o' in 'code'">
            oʊ
           </span>
          </span>
          -/
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
       ),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       officially the
       <b>
        Republic of Trinidad and Tobago
       </b>
       , is a twin island
       <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">
        sovereign state
       </a>
       that is the southernmost nation in the
       <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">
        Caribbean
       </a>
       . It is situated 130 kilometres (81 miles) south of
       <a href="/wiki/Grenada" title="Grenada">
        Grenada
       </a>
       off the northern edge of the
       <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">
        South American
       </a>
       mainland, 11 kilometres (6.8 miles) off the coast of northeastern
       <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">
        Venezuela
       </a>
       . It shares
       <a href="/wiki/Maritime_boundary" title="Maritime boundary">
        maritime boundaries
       </a>
       with
       <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">
        Barbados
       </a>
       to the northeast, Grenada to the northwest,
       <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">
        Guyana
       </a>
       to the southeast, and Venezuela to the south and west.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The island of
       <a href="/wiki/Trinidad" title="Trinidad">
        Trinidad
       </a>
       was a
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">
        Spanish colony
       </a>
       from the arrival of
       <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">
        Christopher Columbus
       </a>
       in 1498 until Spanish governor Don
       <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Chac%C3%B3n" title="José María Chacón">
        José María Chacón
       </a>
       surrendered the island to a British fleet under the command of
       <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Abercromby" title="Ralph Abercromby">
        Sir Ralph Abercromby
       </a>
       in 1797.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       During the same period, the island of
       <a href="/wiki/Tobago" title="Tobago">
        Tobago
       </a>
       changed hands among
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">
        Spanish
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/British_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="British colonization of the Americas">
        British
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/French_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="French colonization of the Americas">
        French
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Dutch_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Dutch colonization of the Americas">
        Dutch
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Courland_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Courland colonization of the Americas">
        Courlander
       </a>
       colonizers more times than any other island in the Caribbean. Trinidad and Tobago were ceded to Britain in 1802 under the
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Amiens" title="Treaty of Amiens">
        Treaty of Amiens
       </a>
       as separate states and unified in 1889.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Trinidad and Tobago obtained independence in 1962 and became a republic in 1976.
      </p>
      <p>
       As of 2015
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , Trinidad and Tobago had the third highest
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GDP_per_capita" title="GDP per capita">
        GDP per capita
       </a>
       based on
       <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">
        purchasing power parity
       </a>
       (PPP) in the
       <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">
        Americas
       </a>
       after the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
        United States
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">
        Canada
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is recognised by the
       <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">
        World Bank
       </a>
       as a
       <a href="/wiki/World_Bank_high-income_economy" title="World Bank high-income economy">
        high-income economy
       </a>
       . Unlike most of the English-speaking Caribbean, the country's economy is primarily industrial
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       with an emphasis on petroleum and
       <a href="/wiki/Petrochemical" title="Petrochemical">
        petrochemicals
       </a>
       . The country's wealth is attributed to its large reserves and exploitation of oil and natural gas.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Trinidad and Tobago is known for its
       <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_Carnival" title="Trinidad and Tobago Carnival">
        Carnival
       </a>
       celebration and as the birthplace of
       <a href="/wiki/Steelpan" title="Steelpan">
        steelpan
       </a>
       drums, the
       <a href="/wiki/Limbo_(dance)" title="Limbo (dance)">
        limbo
       </a>
       , and music styles such as
       <a href="/wiki/Calypso_music" title="Calypso music">
        calypso
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Soca_music" title="Soca music">
        soca
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Parang" title="Parang">
        parang
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Chutney_music" title="Chutney music">
        chutney
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cariso" title="Cariso">
        cariso
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Extempo" title="Extempo">
        extempo
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Kaiso" title="Kaiso">
        kaiso
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Pichakaree" title="Pichakaree">
        pichakaree
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Rapso" title="Rapso">
        rapso
       </a>
       . It is also famous for its
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indo-Caribbean" title="Indo-Caribbean">
        Indo-Caribbean
       </a>
       cuisine, such as a
       <a href="/wiki/Curry" title="Curry">
        curry
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Chickpea" title="Chickpea">
        chickpea
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Flatbread" title="Flatbread">
        flatbread
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Sandwich" title="Sandwich">
        sandwich
       </a>
       known as
       <a href="/wiki/Doubles_(food)" title="Doubles (food)">
        doubles
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">
        Etymology
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Historian
       <a href="/wiki/Edward_Lanzer_Joseph" title="Edward Lanzer Joseph">
        E. L. Joseph
       </a>
       claimed that Trinidad's Amerindian name was
       <i>
        Cairi
       </i>
       or "Land of the
       <a href="/wiki/Hummingbird" title="Hummingbird">
        Humming Bird
       </a>
       ", derived from the
       <a href="/wiki/Arawak_language" title="Arawak language">
        Arawak
       </a>
       name for hummingbird,
       <i>
        ierèttê
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        yerettê
       </i>
       . However, Boomert claims that neither
       <i>
        cairi
       </i>
       nor
       <i>
        caeri
       </i>
       means hummingbird and
       <i>
        tukusi
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        tucuchi
       </i>
       does.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
          <span title="Why are 'cairi' and 'caeri' suddenly being mentioned? What does this have to do with the preceding? (August 2012)">
           clarification needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boomert_20-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Boomert-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Others have reported that
       <i>
        kairi
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        iere
       </i>
       simply mean
       <i>
        island
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2009)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">
        Christopher Columbus
       </a>
       renamed it "La Isla de la Trinidad" ("The Island of the
       <a href="/wiki/Trinity" title="Trinity">
        Trinity
       </a>
       "), fulfilling a vow made before setting out on his third voyage of exploration.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hart,_Marie_1965_p._13_21-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Hart,_Marie_1965_p._13-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Tobago's cigar-like shape may have given it its Spanish name (
       <i>
        cabaco
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        tavaco
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        tobacco
       </i>
       ) and possibly its Amerindian names of Aloubaéra (black conch) and Urupaina (big snail),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boomert_20-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Boomert-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       although the English pronunciation is
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /təˈbeɪɡoʊ/
       </span>
       , rhyming with
       <i>
        lumbago
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        sago
       </i>
       , and "may go".
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2009)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">
        Geography
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Geography of Trinidad and Tobago">
        Geography of Trinidad and Tobago
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Td-map.gif">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="367" data-file-width="342" height="322" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Td-map.gif/300px-Td-map.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/01/Td-map.gif 1.5x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Td-map.gif" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A map of Trinidad and Tobago
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Trinidad_Topography.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="1750" height="292" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Trinidad_Topography.png/300px-Trinidad_Topography.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Trinidad_Topography.png/450px-Trinidad_Topography.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Trinidad_Topography.png/600px-Trinidad_Topography.png 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Trinidad_Topography.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Trinidad and Tobago's topography
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Trinidad and Tobago are islands situated between 10° 2' and 11° 12' N
       <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">
        latitude
       </a>
       and 60° 30' and 61° 56' W
       <a href="/wiki/Longitude" title="Longitude">
        longitude
       </a>
       . At the closest point, Trinidad is just 11 kilometres (6.8 mi) from
       <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">
        Venezuelan
       </a>
       territory. Covering an area of 5,128 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       (1,980 sq mi),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-back_22-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-back-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the country consists of the two main islands, Trinidad and Tobago, and numerous smaller landforms, including
       <a href="/wiki/Chacachacare" title="Chacachacare">
        Chacachacare
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Monos" title="Monos">
        Monos
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Huevos" title="Huevos">
        Huevos
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Gaspar_Grande" title="Gaspar Grande">
        Gaspar Grande
       </a>
       (or Gasparee),
       <a href="/wiki/Little_Tobago" title="Little Tobago">
        Little Tobago
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Giles_Island" title="Saint Giles Island">
        St. Giles Island
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Trinidad is 4,768 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       (1,841 sq mi) in area (comprising 93.0% of the country's total area) with an average length of 80 km (50 mi) and an average width of 59 kilometres (37 mi). Tobago has an area of about 300 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       (120 sq mi), or 5.8% of the country's area, is 41 km (25 mi) long and 12 km (7.5 mi) at its greatest width. Trinidad and Tobago lie on the continental shelf of South America, and are thus geologically considered to lie entirely in South America.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mayaro_Beach;_Trinidad_%26_Tobago.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Mayaro_Beach%3B_Trinidad_%26_Tobago.jpg/220px-Mayaro_Beach%3B_Trinidad_%26_Tobago.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Mayaro_Beach%3B_Trinidad_%26_Tobago.jpg/330px-Mayaro_Beach%3B_Trinidad_%26_Tobago.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Mayaro_Beach%3B_Trinidad_%26_Tobago.jpg/440px-Mayaro_Beach%3B_Trinidad_%26_Tobago.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mayaro_Beach;_Trinidad_%26_Tobago.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Mayaro,_Trinidad" title="Mayaro, Trinidad">
          Mayaro
         </a>
         Beach, in the southeastern area of Trinidad
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The terrain of the islands is a mixture of mountains and plains. The highest point in the country is found on the
       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Range" title="Northern Range">
        Northern Range
       </a>
       at
       <a href="/wiki/El_Cerro_del_Aripo" title="El Cerro del Aripo">
        El Cerro del Aripo
       </a>
       , which is 940 metres (3,080 ft) above sea level.
      </p>
      <p>
       As the majority of the population live in the island of Trinidad, this is the location of most major towns and cities. There are four major municipalities in Trinidad:
       <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Spain" title="Port of Spain">
        Port of Spain
       </a>
       , the capital,
       <a href="/wiki/San_Fernando,_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="San Fernando, Trinidad and Tobago">
        San Fernando
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Arima" title="Arima">
        Arima
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Chaguanas" title="Chaguanas">
        Chaguanas
       </a>
       . The main town in Tobago is
       <a href="/wiki/Scarborough,_Tobago" title="Scarborough, Tobago">
        Scarborough
       </a>
       . Trinidad is made up of a variety of soil types, the majority being fine sands and heavy clays. The alluvial valleys of the Northern Range and the soils of the
       <a href="/wiki/East-West_Corridor" title="East-West Corridor">
        East-West Corridor
       </a>
       are the most fertile.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">
        Geology
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Geology">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The Northern Range consists mainly of Upper
       <a href="/wiki/Jurassic" title="Jurassic">
        Jurassic
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Cretaceous" title="Cretaceous">
        Cretaceous
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Metamorphic_rock" title="Metamorphic rock">
        metamorphic rocks
       </a>
       . The Northern Lowlands (
       <a href="/wiki/East-West_Corridor" title="East-West Corridor">
        East-West Corridor
       </a>
       and Caroni Plains) consist of younger shallow marine
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clastic_sediment" title="Clastic sediment">
        clastic sediments
       </a>
       . South of this, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_Range,_Trinidad" title="Central Range, Trinidad">
        Central Range
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Fold_and_thrust_belt" title="Fold and thrust belt">
        fold and thrust belt
       </a>
       consists of Cretaceous and
       <a href="/wiki/Eocene" title="Eocene">
        Eocene
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Sedimentary_rock" title="Sedimentary rock">
        sedimentary rocks
       </a>
       , with
       <a href="/wiki/Miocene" title="Miocene">
        Miocene
       </a>
       formations along the southern and eastern flanks. The Naparima Plains and the
       <a href="/wiki/Nariva_Swamp" title="Nariva Swamp">
        Nariva Swamp
       </a>
       form the southern shoulder of this uplift.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Southern Lowlands consist of Miocene and
       <a href="/wiki/Pliocene" title="Pliocene">
        Pliocene
       </a>
       sands, clays, and gravels. These overlie oil and
       <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">
        natural gas
       </a>
       deposits, especially north of the Los Bajos Fault. The Southern Range forms the third
       <a href="/wiki/Anticline" title="Anticline">
        anticlinal
       </a>
       uplift. It consists of several chains of hills, most famous being the
       <a href="/wiki/Trinity_Hills" title="Trinity Hills">
        Trinity Hills
       </a>
       . The rocks consist of
       <a href="/wiki/Sandstone" title="Sandstone">
        sandstones
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Shale" title="Shale">
        shales
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Siltstone" title="Siltstone">
        siltstones
       </a>
       and clays formed in the Miocene and uplifted in the
       <a href="/wiki/Pleistocene" title="Pleistocene">
        Pleistocene
       </a>
       .
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tar_sands" title="Tar sands">
        Oil sands
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Mud_volcano" title="Mud volcano">
        mud volcanoes
       </a>
       are especially common in this area.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">
        Climate
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Climate">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The climate is tropical. There are two seasons annually: the
       <a href="/wiki/Dry_season" title="Dry season">
        dry season
       </a>
       for the first five months of the year, and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rainy_season" title="Rainy season">
        rainy season
       </a>
       in the remaining seven of the year. Winds are predominantly from the northeast and are dominated by the northeast
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trade_wind" title="Trade wind">
        trade winds
       </a>
       . Unlike most of the other Caribbean islands, both Trinidad and Tobago have frequently escaped the wrath of major devastating hurricanes, including
       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ivan" title="Hurricane Ivan">
        Hurricane Ivan
       </a>
       , the most powerful storm to have passed close to the islands in recent history, in September 2004. In the Northern Range, the climate is often different in contrast to the sweltering heat of the plains below. With constant cloud and mist cover, and heavy rains in the mountains, the temperature is much cooler.
      </p>
      <p>
       Record temperatures for Trinidad and Tobago are 39 °C (102 °F)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       for the high in Port of Spain, and a low of 12 °C (54 °F).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">
        Biodiversity
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Biodiversity">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ecology_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Ecology of Trinidad and Tobago">
        Ecology of Trinidad and Tobago
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Leatherback_sea_turtle_Tinglar,_USVI_(5839996547).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1085" data-file-width="1864" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Leatherback_sea_turtle_Tinglar%2C_USVI_%285839996547%29.jpg/220px-Leatherback_sea_turtle_Tinglar%2C_USVI_%285839996547%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Leatherback_sea_turtle_Tinglar%2C_USVI_%285839996547%29.jpg/330px-Leatherback_sea_turtle_Tinglar%2C_USVI_%285839996547%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Leatherback_sea_turtle_Tinglar%2C_USVI_%285839996547%29.jpg/440px-Leatherback_sea_turtle_Tinglar%2C_USVI_%285839996547%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Leatherback_sea_turtle_Tinglar,_USVI_(5839996547).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Trinidad and Tobago is a major nesting site for
         <a href="/wiki/Leatherback_sea_turtle" title="Leatherback sea turtle">
          Leatherback Turtles
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Because Trinidad and Tobago lie on the continental shelf of South America, their biological diversity is unlike that of most other Caribbean islands, and has much in common with that of
       <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">
        Venezuela
       </a>
       . The main ecosystems are: coastal and marine (coral reefs, mangrove swamps, open ocean and seagrass beds); forest; freshwater (rivers and streams);
       <a href="/wiki/Karst" title="Karst">
        karst
       </a>
       ; man-made ecosystems (agricultural land, freshwater dams, secondary forest); and savanna. On 1 August 1996, Trinidad and Tobago ratified the 1992 Rio
       <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_Biological_Diversity" title="Convention on Biological Diversity">
        Convention on Biological Diversity
       </a>
       , and it has produced a biodiversity action plan and four reports describing the country's contribution to biodiversity conservation. The reports formally acknowledged the importance of biodiversity to the well-being of the country's people through provision of ecosystem services.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Information about vertebrates is good, with 472 bird species (2 endemics), about 100 mammals, about 90 reptiles (a few endemics), about 30 amphibians (a few endemics), 50 freshwater fish and at least 950 marine fish.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Convention_on_Biological_Diversity_27-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Convention_on_Biological_Diversity-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Information about invertebrates is dispersed and very incomplete. About 650 butterflies,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Convention_on_Biological_Diversity_27-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Convention_on_Biological_Diversity-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       at least 672 beetles (from Tobago alone)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and 40 corals
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Convention_on_Biological_Diversity_27-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Convention_on_Biological_Diversity-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       have been recorded.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Convention_on_Biological_Diversity_27-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-Convention_on_Biological_Diversity-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Although the list is far from complete, 1647 species of fungi, including lichens, have been recorded.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The true total number of fungi is likely to be far higher, given the generally accepted estimate that only about 7% of all fungi worldwide have so far been discovered.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A first effort to estimate the number of endemic fungi tentatively listed 407 species.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Information about micro-organisms is dispersed and very incomplete. Nearly 200 species of marine algae have been recorded.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Convention_on_Biological_Diversity_27-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-Convention_on_Biological_Diversity-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The true total number of micro-organism species must be much higher.
      </p>
      <p>
       Thanks to a recently published checklist, plant diversity in Trinidad and Tobago is well documented with about 3,300 species (59 endemic) recorded.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Convention_on_Biological_Diversity_27-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-Convention_on_Biological_Diversity-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="History of Trinidad and Tobago">
        History of Trinidad and Tobago
       </a>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">
        Prehistory
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Prehistory">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tobago_jade_ceremonial_ax.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1728" data-file-width="2304" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Tobago_jade_ceremonial_ax.jpg/220px-Tobago_jade_ceremonial_ax.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Tobago_jade_ceremonial_ax.jpg/330px-Tobago_jade_ceremonial_ax.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Tobago_jade_ceremonial_ax.jpg/440px-Tobago_jade_ceremonial_ax.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tobago_jade_ceremonial_ax.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Greenstone_(archaeology)" title="Greenstone (archaeology)">
          Greenstone
         </a>
         ceremonial axe, Mount Irvine Bay, Tobago
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Both Trinidad and Tobago were originally settled by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amerindian" title="Amerindian">
        Amerindians
       </a>
       of South American origin. Trinidad was first settled by pre-agricultural Archaic people at least 7,000 years ago, making it the earliest settled part of the Caribbean. Ceramic-using agriculturalists settled Trinidad around 250 BC, and then moved further up the
       <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">
        Lesser Antillean chain
       </a>
       . It was known as 'Land of the
       <a href="/wiki/Hummingbird" title="Hummingbird">
        Humming Bird
       </a>
       ' by the indigenous peoples. At the time of
       <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">
        European
       </a>
       contact, Trinidad was occupied by various
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arawakan" title="Arawakan">
        Arawakan
       </a>
       -speaking groups including the Nepoya and Suppoya, and
       <a href="/wiki/Cariban_languages" title="Cariban languages">
        Cariban
       </a>
       -speaking groups such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Yao_language_(Trinidad)" title="Yao language (Trinidad)">
        Yao
       </a>
       , while Tobago was occupied by the
       <a href="/wiki/Island_Caribs" title="Island Caribs">
        Island Caribs
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galibi" title="Galibi">
        Galibi
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Age_of_Discovery">
        Age of Discovery
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Age of Discovery">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Moruga_-_Christopher_Columbus_monument.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2064" data-file-width="3670" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Moruga_-_Christopher_Columbus_monument.jpg/220px-Moruga_-_Christopher_Columbus_monument.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Moruga_-_Christopher_Columbus_monument.jpg/330px-Moruga_-_Christopher_Columbus_monument.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Moruga_-_Christopher_Columbus_monument.jpg/440px-Moruga_-_Christopher_Columbus_monument.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Moruga_-_Christopher_Columbus_monument.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">
          Christopher Columbus
         </a>
         monument at
         <a href="/wiki/Moruga" title="Moruga">
          Moruga
         </a>
         . Columbus landed here on his third voyage in 1498.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Columbus reported seeing Tobago on the distant horizon in 1498, naming it
       <i>
        Bellaforma
       </i>
       , but did not land on the island.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The present name of Tobago is thought to be a corruption of its old name, "Tobaco".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hart,_Marie_1965_p._13_21-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Hart,_Marie_1965_p._13-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Prise_de_Tobago_1781_par_les_Francais.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="607" data-file-width="640" height="209" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Prise_de_Tobago_1781_par_les_Francais.jpg/220px-Prise_de_Tobago_1781_par_les_Francais.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Prise_de_Tobago_1781_par_les_Francais.jpg/330px-Prise_de_Tobago_1781_par_les_Francais.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Prise_de_Tobago_1781_par_les_Francais.jpg/440px-Prise_de_Tobago_1781_par_les_Francais.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Prise_de_Tobago_1781_par_les_Francais.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/French_colonial_empire" title="French colonial empire">
          French
         </a>
         attack on the British island of Tobago in 1781
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Dutch and the
       <a href="/wiki/Courland" title="Courland">
        Courlanders
       </a>
       (people from the small
       <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Courland_and_Semigallia" title="Duchy of Courland and Semigallia">
        Duchy of Courland and Semigallia
       </a>
       belonging to Polish Commonwealth – modern-day
       <a href="/wiki/Latvia" title="Latvia">
        Latvia
       </a>
       ) established themselves in Tobago in the 16th and 17th centuries and produced tobacco and cotton. Over the centuries, Tobago changed hands between
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">
        Spanish
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/British_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="British colonization of the Americas">
        British
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/French_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="French colonization of the Americas">
        French
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Dutch_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Dutch colonization of the Americas">
        Dutch
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Courland_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Courland colonization of the Americas">
        Courlander
       </a>
       colonizers. Britain consolidated its hold on both islands during the
       <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">
        Napoleonic Wars
       </a>
       , and they were combined into the
       <a href="/wiki/Colony" title="Colony">
        colony
       </a>
       of Trinidad and Tobago in 1889.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WDL_35-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-WDL-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       As a result of these colonial struggles, Amerindian, Spanish, French and English
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="List of cities in Trinidad and Tobago">
        place names
       </a>
       are all common in the country.
       <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">
        African
       </a>
       slaves and Chinese,
       <a href="/wiki/Indian_people" title="Indian people">
        Indian
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tamil_people" title="Tamil people">
        Tamil
       </a>
       and free African
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indentured_servant" title="Indentured servant">
        indentured labourers
       </a>
       , as well as
       <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">
        Portuguese
       </a>
       from Madeira, arrived to supply labour in the 19th and early 20th centuries. Emigration from
       <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">
        Barbados
       </a>
       and the other Lesser Antilles,
       <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">
        Venezuela
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">
        Syria
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">
        Lebanon
       </a>
       also impacted on the ethnic make-up of the country.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish_settlement">
        Spanish settlement
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Spanish settlement">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">
        Christopher Columbus
       </a>
       encountered the island of Trinidad on 31 July 1498. In the 1530s, Antonio de Sedeño, a Spanish soldier intent on conquering the island of Trinidad, landed on its southwest coast with a small army of men. He intended to subdue the Orinoco and the Warao, the two major Amerindian peoples of the island, and rule over them in the name of the Spanish king. Sedeño and his men fought the native Carib Indians on many occasions, and subsequently built a fort. The next few decades were generally spent in warfare with the natives, until in 1592, the 'Cacique' (native chief) Wannawanare (also known as Guanaguanare) granted the area later known as "St. Josephs" to Domingo de Vera e Ibargüen, and withdrew to another part of the island.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boomert_20-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Boomert-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The settlement of San José de Oruña (St. Joseph) was established by Antonio de Berrío on this land. Only a couple of years later,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sir_Walter_Raleigh" title="Sir Walter Raleigh">
        Sir Walter Raleigh
       </a>
       arrived in Trinidad on 22 March 1595. He was in search of the long-rumoured "
       <a href="/wiki/El_Dorado" title="El Dorado">
        City of Gold
       </a>
       " supposedly located in South America. He soon attacked San José, captured and interrogated Antonio de Berrío, and obtained much information from him and from the Cacique Topiawari. Raleigh then went on his way, and the Spanish authority was restored.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Raleigh_at_Trinidad.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="412" data-file-width="550" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Raleigh_at_Trinidad.jpg/220px-Raleigh_at_Trinidad.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Raleigh_at_Trinidad.jpg/330px-Raleigh_at_Trinidad.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Raleigh_at_Trinidad.jpg/440px-Raleigh_at_Trinidad.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Raleigh_at_Trinidad.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Walter_Raleigh" title="Walter Raleigh">
          Sir Walter Raleigh
         </a>
         raiding Spanish settlement in Trinidad in 1595
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The next century (the 1600s) passed without major incident but sustained attempts by the Spaniards to control and rule over the Amerindians, and especially the exertions of the missionaries, were preparing grounds for an outburst. In 1687, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholic" title="Catholic">
        Catholic
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catalan_people" title="Catalan people">
        Catalan
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Capuchin_friars" title="Capuchin friars">
        Capuchin friars
       </a>
       were given responsibility for
       <a href="/wiki/Religious_conversion" title="Religious conversion">
        the conversions
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">
        indigenous people
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Trinidad" title="Trinidad">
        Trinidad
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guianas" title="Guianas">
        Guianas
       </a>
       . After 1687, they founded several missions in Trinidad, supported and richly funded by the state, which also granted
       <a href="/wiki/Encomienda" title="Encomienda">
        encomienda
       </a>
       over the native people to them. One such mission was
       <i>
        Santa Rosa de Arima,
       </i>
       established in 1789, when Amerindians from the former
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Encomienda" title="Encomienda">
         encomiendas
        </a>
       </i>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Tacarigua" title="Tacarigua">
        Tacarigua
       </a>
       and
       <i>
        Arauca
       </i>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Arouca,_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Arouca, Trinidad and Tobago">
        Arouca
       </a>
       ) were relocated further west.
      </p>
      <p>
       The missions aimed at conversion and cultural deracination, which were naturally unwelcome to the target population. Escalating tensions between the Spaniards and Amerindians culminated in the
       <a href="/wiki/Arena_Massacre" title="Arena Massacre">
        Arena Massacre
       </a>
       which took place in 1699. Amerindians bound to the Church's
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Encomienda" title="Encomienda">
         encomienda
        </a>
       </i>
       at the mission at Arena/Arima revolted, killing the priests and desecrating the church. They then ambushed the governor and his party, who were on their way to visit the church. The uprising resulted in the death of several hundred Amerindians, of the Roman Catholic priests connected with the mission of San Francisco de los Arenales, of the Spanish Governor
       <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_de_Le%C3%B3n_y_Echales" title="José de León y Echales">
        José de León y Echales
       </a>
       and of all but one member of his party. Among those killed in the governor's party was Juan Mazien de Sotomayor, missionary priest to the Nepuyo villages of Cuara, Tacarigua and Arauca.
      </p>
      <p>
       Order was eventually restored and the Spanish authority was re-established. Another century passed, and during the 1700s, Trinidad was an island province belonging to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_New_Spain" title="Viceroyalty of New Spain">
        Viceroyalty of New Spain
       </a>
       , together with Central America, present-day Mexico and the Southwestern United States.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Besson,_2000_36-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Besson,_2000-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, Trinidad in this period was still mostly forest, populated by a few Spaniards with their handful of slaves and a few thousand Amerindians.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Besson,_2000_36-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Besson,_2000-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Indeed, the population in 1777 was only 1400, and Spanish colonisation in Trinidad remained tenuous.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Influx_of_French_people">
        Influx of French people
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Influx of French people">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jose_Maria_Chacon.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="541" height="257" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Jose_Maria_Chacon.jpg/220px-Jose_Maria_Chacon.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Jose_Maria_Chacon.jpg/330px-Jose_Maria_Chacon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Jose_Maria_Chacon.jpg/440px-Jose_Maria_Chacon.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jose_Maria_Chacon.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Spanish Governor
         <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Chac%C3%B3n" title="José María Chacón">
          José María Chacón
         </a>
         signed the
         <a href="/wiki/Cedula_of_Population" title="Cedula of Population">
          <i>
           Cédula de Población
          </i>
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Since Trinidad was considered underpopulated, Roume de St. Laurent, a Frenchman living in
       <a href="/wiki/Grenada" title="Grenada">
        Grenada
       </a>
       , was able to obtain a
       <a href="/wiki/Cedula_of_Population" title="Cedula of Population">
        <i>
         Cédula de Población
        </i>
       </a>
       from the Spanish king
       <a href="/wiki/Charles_III_of_Spain" title="Charles III of Spain">
        Charles III
       </a>
       on 4 November 1783. A
       <i>
        Cédula de Población
       </i>
       had previously been granted in 1776 by the king, but had not shown results, and therefore the new Cédula was more generous. It granted free land and tax exemption for 10 years to Roman Catholic foreign settlers who were willing to swear allegiance to the King of Spain.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
        <a href="#cite_note-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The land grant was 30 fanegas (13 hectares/32 acres) for each free man, woman and child and half of that for each slave that they brought with them.
      </p>
      <p>
       It was fortuitous that the Cédula was issued only a few years before the French Revolution. During that period of upheaval, French planters with their slaves, free
       <a href="/wiki/Coloureds" title="Coloureds">
        coloureds
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mulattos" title="Mulattos">
        mulattos
       </a>
       from the neighbouring islands of Martinique,
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia" title="Saint Lucia">
        Saint Lucia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Grenada" title="Grenada">
        Grenada
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">
        Guadeloupe
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Dominica" title="Dominica">
        Dominica
       </a>
       migrated to Trinidad, where they established an agriculture-based economy (sugar and cocoa).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Besson,_2000_36-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Besson,_2000-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       These new immigrants established local communities in
       <a href="/wiki/Blanchisseuse" title="Blanchisseuse">
        Blanchisseuse
       </a>
       , Champs Fleurs,
       <a href="/wiki/Paramin" title="Paramin">
        Paramin
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Cascade,
       <a href="/wiki/Carenage" title="Carenage">
        Carenage
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Laventille" title="Laventille">
        Laventille
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Trinidad's population jumped to over 15,000 by the end of 1789, from just under 1,400 in 1777. By 1797, the population of
       <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Spain" title="Port of Spain">
        Port of Spain
       </a>
       had increased from under 3,000 to 10,422 in five years, and consisted of people of mixed race, Spaniards, Africans, French republican soldiers, retired pirates and French nobility.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Besson,_2000_36-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-Besson,_2000-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The total population of Trinidad was 17,718, of which 2,151 were of European ancestry, 4,476 were "free blacks and people of colour", 10,009 were slaves and 1,082
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amerindians" title="Amerindians">
        Amerindians
       </a>
       . The sparse settlement and slow rate of population-increase during Spanish rule (and even during British rule) made Trinidad one of the less populated colonies of the West Indies, with the least developed plantation infrastructure.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brereton_39-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Brereton-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="British_rule">
        British rule
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: British rule">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Trinidad_Ralph_Abercromby.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1712" data-file-width="2288" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Trinidad_Ralph_Abercromby.JPG/220px-Trinidad_Ralph_Abercromby.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Trinidad_Ralph_Abercromby.JPG/330px-Trinidad_Ralph_Abercromby.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Trinidad_Ralph_Abercromby.JPG/440px-Trinidad_Ralph_Abercromby.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Trinidad_Ralph_Abercromby.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A medallion showing the capture of Trinidad and Tobago by the
         <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">
          British
         </a>
         in 1797
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Protector_of_Slaves_Office_(Trinidad)_by_Richard_Bridgens.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1183" data-file-width="1920" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Protector_of_Slaves_Office_%28Trinidad%29_by_Richard_Bridgens.jpg/220px-Protector_of_Slaves_Office_%28Trinidad%29_by_Richard_Bridgens.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Protector_of_Slaves_Office_%28Trinidad%29_by_Richard_Bridgens.jpg/330px-Protector_of_Slaves_Office_%28Trinidad%29_by_Richard_Bridgens.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Protector_of_Slaves_Office_%28Trinidad%29_by_Richard_Bridgens.jpg/440px-Protector_of_Slaves_Office_%28Trinidad%29_by_Richard_Bridgens.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Protector_of_Slaves_Office_(Trinidad)_by_Richard_Bridgens.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <i>
          Protector of Slaves Office (Trinidad)
         </i>
         , Richard Bridgens, c. 1833
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 1797, a British force led by General
       <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Abercromby" title="Ralph Abercromby">
        Sir Ralph Abercromby
       </a>
       launched the
       <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Trinidad_(1797)" title="Invasion of Trinidad (1797)">
        invasion of Trinidad
       </a>
       . His squadron sailed through the Bocas and anchored off the coast of
       <a href="/wiki/Chaguaramas,_Trinidad" title="Chaguaramas, Trinidad">
        Chaguaramas
       </a>
       . The Spanish
       <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Chac%C3%B3n" title="José María Chacón">
        Governor Chacón
       </a>
       decided to capitulate without fighting. Trinidad thus became a British
       <a href="/wiki/Crown_colony" title="Crown colony">
        crown colony
       </a>
       , with a French-speaking population and Spanish laws.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Besson,_2000_36-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-Besson,_2000-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       British rule was formalized under the
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Amiens" title="Treaty of Amiens">
        Treaty of Amiens
       </a>
       (1802).
      </p>
      <p>
       British rule led to an influx of settlers from the United Kingdom and the British colonies of the Eastern Caribbean. English, Scots, Irish, German and Italian families arrived. Under British rule, new estates were created and the import of slaves did increase, but this was the period of
       <a href="/wiki/Abolitionism" title="Abolitionism">
        abolitionism
       </a>
       in England and the slave trade was under attack.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brereton_39-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Brereton-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Williams,_Eric_1962_40-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Williams,_Eric_1962-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Slavery was
       <a href="/wiki/Slavery_Abolition_Act_1833" title="Slavery Abolition Act 1833">
        abolished in 1833
       </a>
       , after which former slaves served an "
       <a href="/wiki/Slavery_Abolition_Act_1833#The_Act" title="Slavery Abolition Act 1833">
        apprenticeship
       </a>
       " period which ended on 1 August 1838 with full emancipation. An overview of the populations statistics in 1838, however, clearly reveals the contrast between Trinidad and its neighbouring islands: upon emancipation of the slaves in 1838, Trinidad had only 17,439 slaves, with 80% of slave owners having fewer than 10 slaves each.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Williams,_Eric_1962_40-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Williams,_Eric_1962-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         84–85
        </span>
       </sup>
       In contrast, at twice the size of Trinidad, Jamaica had roughly 360,000 slaves.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
        <a href="#cite_note-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Influx_of_East_Indians">
        Influx of East Indians
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Influx of East Indians">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Newly_arrived_coolies_in_Trinidad.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1380" data-file-width="2077" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Newly_arrived_coolies_in_Trinidad.jpg/220px-Newly_arrived_coolies_in_Trinidad.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Newly_arrived_coolies_in_Trinidad.jpg/330px-Newly_arrived_coolies_in_Trinidad.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Newly_arrived_coolies_in_Trinidad.jpg/440px-Newly_arrived_coolies_in_Trinidad.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Newly_arrived_coolies_in_Trinidad.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Newly arrived
         <a href="/wiki/Indian_indenture_system" title="Indian indenture system">
          indentured East Indian labourers
         </a>
         in Trinidad and Tobago
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       After slaves were emancipated, plantation owners were in severe need of labour. The British authorities filled this need by instituting a system of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indentureship" title="Indentureship">
        indentureship
       </a>
       . Various nationalities were contracted under this system, including East Indians, Chinese and Portuguese. Of these, the East Indians were imported in the largest numbers, starting from 1 May 1845, when 225 Indians were brought in the first shipment to Trinidad on the
       <a href="/wiki/Fatel_Razack" title="Fatel Razack">
        Fatel Razack
       </a>
       , a Muslim-owned vessel.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Indentureship of the East Indians lasted from 1845 to 1917, during which more than 147,000 Indians were brought to Trinidad to work on sugarcane plantations.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
        <a href="#cite_note-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
       They added what was initially the second-largest population grouping to the young nation, and their labour developed previously underdeveloped plantation lands.
      </p>
      <p>
       The indentureship contract was exploitative, such that historians including Hugh Tinker were to call it "a new system of slavery". People were contracted for a period of five years, with a daily wage as low as 25 cents in the early 20th century, and they were guaranteed return passage to India at the end of their contract period. However,
       <a href="/wiki/Coercion" title="Coercion">
        coercive means
       </a>
       were often used to retain labourers, and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indentured_servant" title="Indentured servant">
        indentureship contracts
       </a>
       were soon extended to 10 years after the planters complained that they were losing their labour too early.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brereton_39-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Brereton-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In lieu of the return passage, the British authorities soon began offering portions of land to encourage settlement; however, the numbers of people who did receive land grants is unclear.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       East Indians entering the colony were also subject to particular crown laws which segregated them from the rest of Trinidad's population, such as the requirement that they carry a pass with them once off the plantations, and that if freed, they carry their "Free Papers" or certificate indicating completion of the indenture period.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
        <a href="#cite_note-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The ex-Indentureds came to constitute a vital and significant section of the population, as did the ex-slaves.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_depression">
        Economic depression
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Economic depression">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Alongside sugarcane, the cacao (
       <a href="/wiki/Cocoa_bean" title="Cocoa bean">
        cocoa
       </a>
       ) crop also contributed greatly to economic earnings in the late nineteenth and early twentieth centuries. In the 1920–1930 period, the collapse of the sugarcane industry concomitant with the failure of the cocoa industry resulted in widespread depression among the rural and agricultural workers in Trinidad, and encouraged the rise of the Labour movement. This movement was led by
       <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Andrew_Cipriani" title="Arthur Andrew Cipriani">
        Arthur Cipriani
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Tubal_Uriah_Butler" title="Tubal Uriah Butler">
        Tubal Uriah "Buzz" Butler
       </a>
       , who, in combination with his Indian partners (notably
       <a href="/wiki/Adrian_Cola_Rienzi" title="Adrian Cola Rienzi">
        Adrian Cola Rienzi
       </a>
       ), aimed to unite the working class and agricultural labour class to achieve a better standard of living for them, as well as to hasten the departure of the British. This effort was severely undermined by the British Home Office and by the British-educated Trinidadian elite, many of whom were descended from the plantocracy themselves. They instigated a vicious race politicking in Trinidad aimed at dividing the class-based movement on race-based lines, and they succeeded, especially since Butler's support had collapsed from the top down.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">
        Petroleum
       </a>
       had been discovered in 1857, but became economically significant only in the 1930s and afterwards,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WDL_35-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-WDL-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       as a result of the collapse of sugarcane and cocoa, and increasing industrialization. By the 1950s, petroleum had become a staple in Trinidad's export market, and was responsible for a growing middle class among all sections of the Trinidad population. The collapse of Trinidad's major agricultural commodities, followed by the Depression, and the rise of the oil economy, led to major changes in the country's social structure.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Independence">
        Independence
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Independence">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Prime_Minister_Dr._Eric_Williams_of_Trinidad_%26_Tobago_(cropped).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1118" data-file-width="907" height="210" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Prime_Minister_Dr._Eric_Williams_of_Trinidad_%26_Tobago_%28cropped%29.jpg/170px-Prime_Minister_Dr._Eric_Williams_of_Trinidad_%26_Tobago_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Prime_Minister_Dr._Eric_Williams_of_Trinidad_%26_Tobago_%28cropped%29.jpg/255px-Prime_Minister_Dr._Eric_Williams_of_Trinidad_%26_Tobago_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Prime_Minister_Dr._Eric_Williams_of_Trinidad_%26_Tobago_%28cropped%29.jpg/340px-Prime_Minister_Dr._Eric_Williams_of_Trinidad_%26_Tobago_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Prime_Minister_Dr._Eric_Williams_of_Trinidad_%26_Tobago_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Eric_Williams" title="Eric Williams">
          Eric Williams
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Trinidad started to gain rights in the early 1900s. They achieved the right to vote in 1924. In the 1940s the citizens pushed for a self run internal government.
      </p>
      <p>
       Trinidad and Tobago gained its independence from the United Kingdom on 31 August 1962.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WDL_35-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-WDL-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">
        Elizabeth II
       </a>
       remained head of state as
       <a href="/wiki/Queen_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Queen of Trinidad and Tobago">
        Queen of Trinidad and Tobago
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Eric_Williams" title="Eric Williams">
        Eric Williams
       </a>
       , a noted Caribbean historian, widely regarded as
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Father_of_the_Nation" title="Father of the Nation">
         The Father of The Nation
        </a>
       </i>
       , was the first
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Prime_Ministers_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="List of Prime Ministers of Trinidad and Tobago">
        Prime Minister
       </a>
       ; he served from 1956 to 1959, before independence as Chief Minister, from 1959 to 1962, before independence as Premier, from 1962 to 1976, after independence as Prime Minister of
       <a href="/wiki/Dominion_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Dominion of Trinidad and Tobago">
        Trinidad and Tobago
       </a>
       , then from 1976 to his death in 1981 as Prime Minister of the Republic of Trinidad and Tobago.
       <a href="/wiki/Rudranath_Capildeo" title="Rudranath Capildeo">
        Rudranath Capildeo
       </a>
       was the first
       <a href="/wiki/Leader_of_the_Opposition_(Trinidad_and_Tobago)" title="Leader of the Opposition (Trinidad and Tobago)">
        Leader of the Opposition
       </a>
       post-independence; he served from 1962 to 1967.
      </p>
      <p>
       The presence of American
       <a href="/wiki/Destroyers_for_Bases_Agreement" title="Destroyers for Bases Agreement">
        military bases
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Chaguaramas,_Trinidad" title="Chaguaramas, Trinidad">
        Chaguaramas
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Cumuto" title="Cumuto">
        Cumuto
       </a>
       in Trinidad during
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">
        World War II
       </a>
       profoundly changed the character of society. In the post-war period, the wave of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Decolonisation" title="Decolonisation">
        decolonisation
       </a>
       that swept the
       <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">
        British Empire
       </a>
       led to the formation of the
       <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_Federation" title="West Indies Federation">
        West Indies Federation
       </a>
       in 1958 as a vehicle for independence. Chaguaramas was the proposed site for the federal capital. The Federation dissolved after the Jamaican Federation of the West Indies
       <a href="/wiki/Jamaican_Federation_of_the_West_Indies_membership_referendum,_1961" title="Jamaican Federation of the West Indies membership referendum, 1961">
        membership referendum
       </a>
       of 1961, and the resulting withdrawal of the
       <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">
        Province of Jamaica
       </a>
       . The government of Trinidad and Tobago then also chose to seek independence from the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">
        United Kingdom
       </a>
       on its own.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
        <a href="#cite_note-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rudranath_Capildeo.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="392" data-file-width="254" height="262" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Rudranath_Capildeo.jpg/170px-Rudranath_Capildeo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/f/fb/Rudranath_Capildeo.jpg 1.5x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rudranath_Capildeo.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Rudranath_Capildeo" title="Rudranath Capildeo">
          Rudranath Capildeo
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 1976, the country became a
       <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">
        republic
       </a>
       within the
       <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">
        Commonwealth
       </a>
       , though it retained the
       <a href="/wiki/Judicial_Committee_of_the_Privy_Council" title="Judicial Committee of the Privy Council">
        Judicial Committee of the Privy Council
       </a>
       as its final appellate court. Between the years 1972 and 1983, the republic profited greatly from the rising price of
       <a href="/wiki/Oil" title="Oil">
        oil
       </a>
       , as the
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_proven_oil_reserves" title="List of countries by proven oil reserves">
        oil-rich country
       </a>
       increased its living standards greatly. In 1990, 114 members of the
       <a href="/wiki/Jamaat_al_Muslimeen" title="Jamaat al Muslimeen">
        Jamaat al Muslimeen
       </a>
       , led by
       <a href="/wiki/Yasin_Abu_Bakr" title="Yasin Abu Bakr">
        Yasin Abu Bakr
       </a>
       , formerly known as Lennox Phillip, stormed the
       <a href="/wiki/The_Red_House_(Trinidad_and_Tobago)" title="The Red House (Trinidad and Tobago)">
        Red House
       </a>
       (the seat of
       <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Parliament of Trinidad and Tobago">
        Parliament
       </a>
       ), and
       <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_Television" title="Trinidad and Tobago Television">
        Trinidad and Tobago Television
       </a>
       , the only television station in the country at the time, and
       <a href="/wiki/Jamaat_al_Muslimeen_coup_attempt" title="Jamaat al Muslimeen coup attempt">
        held the country's government hostage for six days
       </a>
       before surrendering.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
        <a href="#cite_note-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Since 2003, the country has entered a second oil boom, a driving force which the government hopes to use to turn the country's main export back to sugar and
       <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">
        agriculture
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2011)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Great concern was raised in August 2007 when it was predicted that this boom would last only until 2018. Petroleum, petrochemicals and
       <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">
        natural gas
       </a>
