           </div>
          </td>
          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">
           18.1%
          </td>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">
           None/not shared
          </td>
          <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
           <div style="background:grey; width:13.3%; overflow: hidden;">
           </div>
          </td>
          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">
           13.3%
          </td>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">
           <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">
            Islam
           </a>
          </td>
          <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
           <div style="background:green; width:5.0%; overflow: hidden;">
           </div>
          </td>
          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">
           5.0%
          </td>
         </tr>
        </table>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Many different religions are practised in Trinidad and Tobago. According to the 2011 census,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
        <a href="#cite_note-73">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholics" title="Roman Catholics">
        Roman Catholics
       </a>
       were the largest religious group in Trinidad and Tobago with 21.60% of the total population.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hindus" title="Hindus">
        Hindus
       </a>
       were the second largest group with 18.15%, while the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pentecostal" title="Pentecostal">
        Pentecostal
       </a>
       /
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evangelical" title="Evangelical">
        Evangelical
       </a>
       /
       <a href="/wiki/Full_Gospel" title="Full Gospel">
        Full Gospel
       </a>
       denominations were the third largest group with 12.02% of the population. Significantly, respondents who did not state a religious affiliation represented 11.1% of the population. The remaining population is made of
       <a href="/wiki/Spiritual_Baptist" title="Spiritual Baptist">
        Spiritual
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shouter_Baptist" title="Shouter Baptist">
        Shouter
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Baptists" title="Baptists">
        Baptists
       </a>
       (5.67%),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglicans" title="Anglicans">
        Anglicans
       </a>
       (5.67%),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">
        Muslims
       </a>
       (4.97%),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventists" title="Seventh-day Adventists">
        Seventh-day Adventists
       </a>
       (4.09%),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Presbyterians" title="Presbyterians">
        Presbyterians
       </a>
       or
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Congregationalists" title="Congregationalists">
        Congregationalists
       </a>
       (2.49%),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irreligious" title="Irreligious">
        Irreligious
       </a>
       (2.18%),
       <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">
        Jehovah's Witnesses
       </a>
       (1.47%), other
       <a href="/wiki/Baptists" title="Baptists">
        Baptists
       </a>
       (1.21%),
       <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_Orisha" title="Trinidad Orisha">
        Trinidad Orisha
       </a>
       believers (0.9%),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Methodists" title="Methodists">
        Methodists
       </a>
       (0.65%),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rastafarians" title="Rastafarians">
        Rastafarians
       </a>
       (0.27%) and the
       <a href="/wiki/Moravian_Church" title="Moravian Church">
        Moravian Church
       </a>
       (0.27%).
      </p>
      <p>
       Two
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_culture" title="African culture">
        African
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Syncretic" title="Syncretic">
        syncretic
       </a>
       faiths, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shouter_Baptist" title="Shouter Baptist">
        Shouter
       </a>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/Spiritual_Baptist" title="Spiritual Baptist">
        Spiritual Baptists
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_Orisha" title="Trinidad Orisha">
        Orisha
       </a>
       faith (formerly called
       <a href="/wiki/Shango" title="Shango">
        Shangos
       </a>
       , a less than complimentary term)
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       are among the fastest growing religious groups. Similarly, there is a noticeable increase in numbers of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evangelical_Protestant" title="Evangelical Protestant">
        Evangelical Protestant
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fundamentalist_Christian" title="Fundamentalist Christian">
        Fundamentalist
       </a>
       churches usually lumped as "
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pentecostal" title="Pentecostal">
        Pentecostal
       </a>
       " by most Trinidadians, although this designation is often inaccurate.
       <a href="/wiki/Sikhism" title="Sikhism">
        Sikhism
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Jainism" title="Jainism">
        Jainism
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Zoroastrianism" title="Zoroastrianism">
        Zoroastrianism
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD" title="Bahá'í">
        Bahá'í
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">
        Buddhism
       </a>
       are practiced by a minority of
       <a href="/wiki/Indo-Trinidadian_and_Tobagonian" title="Indo-Trinidadian and Tobagonian">
        Indo-Trinidadian and Tobagonians
       </a>
       . Several eastern religions such as
       <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">
        Buddhism
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Taoism" title="Taoism">
        Taoism
       </a>
       are followed by the
       <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Trinidadian_and_Tobagonian" title="Chinese Trinidadian and Tobagonian">
        Chinese community
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Education">
        Education
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Education">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          This section
          <b>
           does not
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">
            cite
           </a>
           any
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
            sources
           </a>
          </b>
          .
          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           Please help
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit">
            improve this section
           </a>
           by
           <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">
            adding citations to reliable sources
           </a>
           . Unsourced material may be challenged and
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
            removed
           </a>
           .
          </span>
          <small>
           <i>
            (August 2017)
           </i>
          </small>
          <small class="hide-when-compact">
           <i>
            (
            <a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">
             Learn how and when to remove this template message
            </a>
            )
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Education in Trinidad and Tobago">
        Education in Trinidad and Tobago
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Children generally start pre-school at two and a half years but this is not mandatory. They are however, expected to have basic reading and writing skills when they commence primary school. Students proceed to a primary school at the age of five years. Seven years are spent in primary school. The seven classes of primary school consists of First Year and Second Year, followed by Standard One through Standard Five. During the final year of primary school, students prepare for and sit the Secondary Entrance Assessment (SEA) which determines the secondary school the child will attend.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TnT_St._Augustine_UWI_Campus.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3240" data-file-width="4320" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/TnT_St._Augustine_UWI_Campus.jpg/220px-TnT_St._Augustine_UWI_Campus.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/TnT_St._Augustine_UWI_Campus.jpg/330px-TnT_St._Augustine_UWI_Campus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/TnT_St._Augustine_UWI_Campus.jpg/440px-TnT_St._Augustine_UWI_Campus.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:TnT_St._Augustine_UWI_Campus.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_West_Indies" title="University of the West Indies">
          University of the West Indies
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Saint_Augustine,_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Saint Augustine, Trinidad and Tobago">
          St. Augustine
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Students attend secondary school for a minimum of five years, leading to the CSEC (Caribbean Secondary Education Certificate) examinations, which is the equivalent of the British GCSE O levels. Children with satisfactory grades may opt to continue high school for a further two-year period, leading to the Caribbean Advanced Proficiency Examinations (CAPE), the equivalent of GCE A levels. Both CSEC and CAPE examinations are held by the Caribbean Examinations Council (CXC). Public Primary and Secondary education is free for all, although private and religious schooling is available for a fee.
      </p>
      <p>
       Tertiary education for tuition costs are provided for via GATE (The Government Assistance for Tuition Expenses), up to the level of the bachelor's degree, at the
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_West_Indies" title="University of the West Indies">
        University of the West Indies
       </a>
       (UWI), the
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="University of Trinidad and Tobago">
        University of Trinidad and Tobago
       </a>
       (UTT), the
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_Southern_Caribbean" title="University of the Southern Caribbean">
        University of the Southern Caribbean
       </a>
       (USC), the
       <a href="/wiki/College_of_Science,_Technology_and_Applied_Arts_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="College of Science, Technology and Applied Arts of Trinidad and Tobago">
        College of Science, Technology and Applied Arts of Trinidad and Tobago
       </a>
       (COSTAATT) and certain other local accredited institutions. Government also currently subsidizes some Masters programmes. Both the Government and the private sector also provide financial assistance in the form of academic scholarships to gifted or needy students for study at local, regional or international universities.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Women">
        Women
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Women">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Women_in_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Women in Trinidad and Tobago">
        Women in Trinidad and Tobago
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Women have a key role in Trinidadian demographics. While women account for only 49% of the population, they constitute nearly 55% of the workforce in the country.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
        <a href="#cite_note-74">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">
        Culture
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Culture">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Culture of Trinidad and Tobago">
        Culture of Trinidad and Tobago
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Orange_Carnival_Masqueraders_in_Trinidad.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Orange_Carnival_Masqueraders_in_Trinidad.jpg/220px-Orange_Carnival_Masqueraders_in_Trinidad.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Orange_Carnival_Masqueraders_in_Trinidad.jpg/330px-Orange_Carnival_Masqueraders_in_Trinidad.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Orange_Carnival_Masqueraders_in_Trinidad.jpg/440px-Orange_Carnival_Masqueraders_in_Trinidad.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Orange_Carnival_Masqueraders_in_Trinidad.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Masqueraders during
         <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_Carnival" title="Trinidad and Tobago Carnival">
          Carnival
         </a>
         celebrations
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:277px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_tadjah_at_Hosay.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="558" data-file-width="508" height="302" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/A_tadjah_at_Hosay.jpg/275px-A_tadjah_at_Hosay.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/A_tadjah_at_Hosay.jpg/413px-A_tadjah_at_Hosay.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/91/A_tadjah_at_Hosay.jpg 2x" width="275"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A_tadjah_at_Hosay.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tadjah" title="Tadjah">
          tadjah
         </a>
         at
         <a href="/wiki/Hosay" title="Hosay">
          Hosay
         </a>
         in
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Port-of-Spain" title="Port-of-Spain">
          Port-of-Spain
         </a>
         during the 1950s
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Trinidad and Tobago claims two
       <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">
        Nobel Prize
       </a>
       -winning authors,
       <a href="/wiki/V._S._Naipaul" title="V. S. Naipaul">
        V. S. Naipaul
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia" title="Saint Lucia">
        St Lucian
       </a>
       -born
       <a href="/wiki/Derek_Walcott" title="Derek Walcott">
        Derek Walcott
       </a>
       (who founded the Trinidad Theatre Workshop, working and raising a family in Trinidad for much of his career). Designer
       <a href="/wiki/Peter_Minshall" title="Peter Minshall">
        Peter Minshall
       </a>
       is renowned not only for his Carnival costumes but also for his role in opening ceremonies of the
       <a href="/wiki/1992_Summer_Olympics" title="1992 Summer Olympics">
        Barcelona Olympics
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/1994_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1994 FIFA World Cup">
        1994 FIFA World Cup
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/1996_Summer_Olympics" title="1996 Summer Olympics">
        1996 Summer Olympics
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/2002_Winter_Olympics" title="2002 Winter Olympics">
        2002 Winter Olympics
       </a>
       , for which he won an
       <a href="/wiki/Emmy_Award" title="Emmy Award">
        Emmy Award
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_Holder" title="Geoffrey Holder">
        Geoffrey Holder
       </a>
       (brother of
       <a href="/wiki/Boscoe_Holder" title="Boscoe Holder">
        Boscoe Holder
       </a>
       ) and
       <a href="/wiki/Heather_Headley" title="Heather Headley">
        Heather Headley
       </a>
       are two Trinidad-born artists who have won
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tony_Awards" title="Tony Awards">
        Tony Awards
       </a>
       for theatre. Holder also has a distinguished film career, and Headley has won a
       <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">
        Grammy Award
       </a>
       as well. Recording artists
       <a href="/wiki/Billy_Ocean" title="Billy Ocean">
        Billy Ocean
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Nicki_Minaj" title="Nicki Minaj">
        Nicki Minaj
       </a>
       are also Trinidadian. Interestingly, three actors who appeared on
       <a href="/wiki/Will_Smith" title="Will Smith">
        Will Smith
       </a>
       's sitcom
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Fresh_Prince_of_Bel-Air" title="The Fresh Prince of Bel-Air">
         The Fresh Prince of Bel-Air
        </a>
       </i>
       are of Trinidadian descent:
       <a href="/wiki/Tatyana_Ali" title="Tatyana Ali">
        Tatyana Ali
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_Ribeiro" title="Alfonso Ribeiro">
        Alfonso Ribeiro
       </a>
       were series regulars as Will's cousins Ashley and Carlton, respectively, while
       <a href="/wiki/Nia_Long" title="Nia Long">
        Nia Long
       </a>
       played Will's girlfriend Lisa.
       <a href="/wiki/Foxy_Brown_(rapper)" title="Foxy Brown (rapper)">
        Foxy Brown
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Dean_Marshall" title="Dean Marshall">
        Dean Marshall
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Sommore" title="Sommore">
        Sommore
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Kareem_Abdul-Jabbar" title="Kareem Abdul-Jabbar">
        Kareem Abdul-Jabbar
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Gabrielle_Reece" title="Gabrielle Reece">
        Gabrielle Reece
       </a>
       , pop singer
       <a href="/wiki/Haddaway" title="Haddaway">
        Haddaway
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tracy_Quan" title="Tracy Quan">
        Tracy Quan
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mike_Bibby" title="Mike Bibby">
        Mike Bibby
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lauryn_Williams" title="Lauryn Williams">
        Lauryn Williams
       </a>
       , Fresh Kid Ice, and
       <a href="/wiki/Roy_Hibbert" title="Roy Hibbert">
        Roy Hibbert
       </a>
       are all of Trinidadian descent.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
        <a href="#cite_note-75">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Trinidad and Tobago also has the distinction of being the smallest country to have two Miss Universe titleholders and the first
       <a href="/wiki/Black_people" title="Black people">
        black
       </a>
       woman ever to win:
       <a href="/wiki/Janelle_Commissiong" title="Janelle Commissiong">
        Janelle Commissiong
       </a>
       in 1977, followed by
       <a href="/wiki/Wendy_Fitzwilliam" title="Wendy Fitzwilliam">
        Wendy Fitzwilliam
       </a>
       in 1998; the country has also had one Miss World titleholder,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Giselle_LaRonde" title="Giselle LaRonde">
        Giselle LaRonde
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Music">
        Music
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Music">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Music of Trinidad and Tobago">
        Music of Trinidad and Tobago
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Theaterspektakel_(2010)_2010-09-04_19-02-50.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Theaterspektakel_%282010%29_2010-09-04_19-02-50.JPG/220px-Theaterspektakel_%282010%29_2010-09-04_19-02-50.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Theaterspektakel_%282010%29_2010-09-04_19-02-50.JPG/330px-Theaterspektakel_%282010%29_2010-09-04_19-02-50.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Theaterspektakel_%282010%29_2010-09-04_19-02-50.JPG/440px-Theaterspektakel_%282010%29_2010-09-04_19-02-50.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Theaterspektakel_(2010)_2010-09-04_19-02-50.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Steelpan" title="Steelpan">
          Steelpan
         </a>
         was invented in Trinidad.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Trinidad and Tobago is the birthplace of
       <a href="/wiki/Calypso_music" title="Calypso music">
        calypso music
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Steelpan" title="Steelpan">
        steelpan
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
        <a href="#cite_note-76">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
        <a href="#cite_note-77">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
        <a href="#cite_note-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Trinidad is also the birthplace of
       <a href="/wiki/Soca_music" title="Soca music">
        soca music
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Chutney_music" title="Chutney music">
        chutney music
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Parang" title="Parang">
        parang
       </a>
       . The diverse cultural and religious backgrounds of its citizens has led to many festivities and ceremonies throughout the year, such as Carnival,
       <a href="/wiki/Diwali" title="Diwali">
        Diwali
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Eid_al-Fitr" title="Eid al-Fitr">
        Eid
       </a>
       festivities.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
        <a href="#cite_note-79">
         [79]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">
        Sports
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Sports">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Olympic_sports">
        Olympic sports
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Olympic sports">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_at_the_Olympics" title="Trinidad and Tobago at the Olympics">
        Trinidad and Tobago at the Olympics
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Hasely_Crawford" title="Hasely Crawford">
        Hasely Crawford
       </a>
       won the first
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olympic_games" title="Olympic games">
        Olympic
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Gold_medal" title="Gold medal">
        gold medal
       </a>
       for Trinidad and Tobago in the men's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/100_meter_dash" title="100 meter dash">
        100 metre dash
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/1976_Summer_Olympics" title="1976 Summer Olympics">
        1976 Summer Olympics
       </a>
       . Nine different athletes from Trinidad and Tobago have won twelve medals at the Olympics, beginning with a
       <a href="/wiki/Silver_medal" title="Silver medal">
        silver medal
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Olympic_weightlifting" title="Olympic weightlifting">
        weightlifting
       </a>
       , won by Rodney Wilkes in
       <a href="/wiki/1948_Summer_Olympics" title="1948 Summer Olympics">
        1948
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
        <a href="#cite_note-80">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and most recently, a gold medal by
       <a href="/wiki/Keshorn_Walcott" title="Keshorn Walcott">
        Keshorn Walcott
       </a>
       in the men's
       <a href="/wiki/Javelin_throw" title="Javelin throw">
        javelin throw
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">
        2012
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Ato_Boldon" title="Ato Boldon">
        Ato Boldon
       </a>
       has won the most Olympic and World Championship medals for Trinidad and Tobago in athletics, with eight in total – four from the Olympics and four from the World Championships. Boldon is the only world champion Trinidad and Tobago has produced to date in athletics. He won the 1997
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/200_meters" title="200 meters">
        200 m sprint
       </a>
       World Championship in
       <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">
        Athens
       </a>
       . Swimmer
       <a href="/wiki/George_Bovell" title="George Bovell">
        George Bovell
       </a>
       III won a bronze medal in the men's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/200_metres_Individual_Medley" title="200 metres Individual Medley">
        200 m IM
       </a>
       in 2004.
      </p>
      <p>
       Also in 2012
       <a href="/wiki/Lalonde_Gordon" title="Lalonde Gordon">
        Lalonde Gordon
       </a>
       competed in the XXX Summer Olympics where he won a Bronze Medal in the 400 metres (1,300 feet), being surpassed by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Luguelin_Santos" title="Luguelin Santos">
        Luguelin Santos
       </a>
       of the Dominican Republic and
       <a href="/wiki/Kirani_James" title="Kirani James">
        Kirani James
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Grenada" title="Grenada">
        Grenada
       </a>
       . Keshorn Walcott (as stated above) came first in javelin and earned a gold medal, making him the second Trinidadian in the country's history to receive one. This also makes him the first Western
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
          <span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (September 2015)">
           clarification needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       athlete in 40 years to receive a gold medal in the javelin sport, and the first athlete from Trinidad and Tobago to win a gold medal in a field event in the Olympics. Sprinter Richard Thompson is also from Trinidad and Tobago. He came second place to Usain Bolt in the Beijing Olympics in the 100 metres (330 feet) with a time of 9.89s.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cricket">
        Cricket
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Cricket">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Cricket_in_the_West_Indies" title="Cricket in the West Indies">
        Cricket in the West Indies
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_national_cricket_team" title="Trinidad and Tobago national cricket team">
        Trinidad and Tobago national cricket team
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BrianLaraUkexpat.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1440" data-file-width="2160" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/BrianLaraUkexpat.jpg/220px-BrianLaraUkexpat.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/BrianLaraUkexpat.jpg/330px-BrianLaraUkexpat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/BrianLaraUkexpat.jpg/440px-BrianLaraUkexpat.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BrianLaraUkexpat.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Brian_Lara" title="Brian Lara">
          Brian Lara
         </a>
         batting for the
         <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_cricket_team" title="West Indies cricket team">
          West Indies
         </a>
         against
         <a href="/wiki/India_national_cricket_team" title="India national cricket team">
          India
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Cricket is a popular sport of Trinidad and Tobago, with intense inter-island rivalry with its Caribbean neighbours. Cricket is the national sport of the country. Trinidad and Tobago is represented at
       <a href="/wiki/Test_cricket" title="Test cricket">
        Test cricket
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/One_Day_International" title="One Day International">
        One Day International
       </a>
       as well as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Twenty20_cricket" title="Twenty20 cricket">
        Twenty20 cricket
       </a>
       level as a member of the
       <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_cricket_team" title="West Indies cricket team">
        West Indies team
       </a>
       . The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_cricket_team" title="Trinidad and Tobago cricket team">
        national team
       </a>
       plays at the
       <a href="/wiki/First-class_cricket" title="First-class cricket">
        first-class
       </a>
       level in regional competitions. Trinidad and Tobago along with other islands from the Caribbean co-hosted the
       <a href="/wiki/2007_Cricket_World_Cup" title="2007 Cricket World Cup">
        2007 Cricket World Cup
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Park_Oval" title="Queen's Park Oval">
        Queen's Park Oval
       </a>
       located in
       <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Spain" title="Port of Spain">
        Port of Spain
       </a>
       is the largest cricket ground in the
       <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">
        West Indies
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Brian_Lara" title="Brian Lara">
        Brian Lara
       </a>
       , world record holder for the most runs scored both in a Test and in a First Class innings and other records, was born in a small town of
       <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz,_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Santa Cruz, Trinidad and Tobago">
        Santa Cruz, Trinidad and Tobago
       </a>
       and is often referred to as the Prince of Port of Spain or simply the Prince. This legendary West Indian batsman is widely regarded (along with Sir Donald Bradman, Sunil Gavaskar and Sachin Tendulkar) as one of the best batsmen ever to have played the game, and is one of the most famous sporting icons in the country.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Football">
        Football
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Football">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Association_football_in_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Association football in Trinidad and Tobago">
        Association football in Trinidad and Tobago
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">
        Association football
       </a>
       is also a popular sport in Trinidad and Tobago.
       <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_national_football_team" title="Trinidad and Tobago national football team">
        The men's national football team
       </a>
       qualified for the
       <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">
        2006 FIFA World Cup
       </a>
       for the first time by beating
       <a href="/wiki/Bahrain_national_football_team" title="Bahrain national football team">
        Bahrain
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Manama" title="Manama">
        Manama
       </a>
       on 16 November 2005, making them the second smallest country ever (in terms of population) to qualify, after
       <a href="/wiki/Iceland_national_football_team" title="Iceland national football team">
        Iceland
       </a>
       . The team, coached by
       <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">
        Dutchman
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Leo_Beenhakker" title="Leo Beenhakker">
        Leo Beenhakker
       </a>
       , and led by Tobagonian-born captain
       <a href="/wiki/Dwight_Yorke" title="Dwight Yorke">
        Dwight Yorke
       </a>
       , drew their first group game – against
       <a href="/wiki/Sweden_national_football_team" title="Sweden national football team">
        Sweden
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Dortmund" title="Dortmund">
        Dortmund
       </a>
       , 0–0, but lost the second game to
       <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">
        England
       </a>
       on late goals, 0–2. They were eliminated after losing 2–0 to
       <a href="/wiki/Paraguay_national_football_team" title="Paraguay national football team">
        Paraguay
       </a>
       in the last game of the Group Stage. Prior to the 2006 World Cup qualification, Trinidad and Tobago came agonizingly close in a controversial qualification campaign for the
       <a href="/wiki/1974_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1974 FIFA World Cup">
        1974 FIFA World Cup
       </a>
       . Following the match, the referee of their critical game against
       <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">
        Haiti
       </a>
       was awarded a lifetime ban for his actions.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
        <a href="#cite_note-81">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Trinidad and Tobago again fell just short of qualifying for the World Cup in
       <a href="/wiki/1990_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1990 FIFA World Cup">
        1990
       </a>
       , needing only a draw at home against the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_men%27s_national_soccer_team" title="United States men's national soccer team">
        United States
       </a>
       but losing 1–0.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
        <a href="#cite_note-82">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
       They play their home matches at the
       <a href="/wiki/Hasely_Crawford_Stadium" title="Hasely Crawford Stadium">
        Hasely Crawford Stadium
       </a>
       . Trinidad and Tobago hosted the
       <a href="/wiki/2001_FIFA_U-17_World_Championship" title="2001 FIFA U-17 World Championship">
        2001 FIFA U-17 World Championship
       </a>
       , and hosted the
       <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_U-17_Women%27s_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA U-17 Women's World Cup">
        2010 FIFA U-17 Women's World Cup
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/TT_Pro_League" title="TT Pro League">
        TT Pro League
       </a>
       is the country's primary football competition and is the top level of the
       <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_football_league_system" title="Trinidad and Tobago football league system">
        Trinidad and Tobago football league system
       </a>
       . The Pro League serves as a league for
       <a href="/wiki/Professional" title="Professional">
        professional
       </a>
       football clubs in Trinidad and Tobago. The league began in 1999 as part of a need for a professional league to strengthen the country's
       <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_national_football_team" title="Trinidad and Tobago national football team">
        national team
       </a>
       and improve the development of domestic players. The first season took place in the same year beginning with eight teams.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Basketball">
        Basketball
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Basketball">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_national_basketball_team" title="Trinidad and Tobago national basketball team">
        Trinidad and Tobago national basketball team
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">
        Basketball
       </a>
       is commonly played in Trinidad and Tobago in colleges, universities and throughout various urban basketball courts. Its national team is one of the most successful teams in the Caribbean. At the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caribbean_Basketball_Championship" title="Caribbean Basketball Championship">
        Caribbean Basketball Championship
       </a>
       it won four straight gold medals from 1986–1990.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_sports">
        Other sports
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Other sports">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Netball" title="Netball">
        Netball
       </a>
       has long been a popular sport in Trinidad and Tobago, although it has declined in popularity in recent years. At the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Netball_World_Championships" title="Netball World Championships">
        Netball World Championships
       </a>
       they co-won the event in 1979, were runners up in 1987, and second runners up in 1983.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union_in_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Rugby union in Trinidad and Tobago">
        Rugby
       </a>
       is played in Trinidad and Tobago and continues to be a popular sport, and
       <a href="/wiki/Horse_racing" title="Horse racing">
        horse racing
       </a>
       is regularly followed in the country.
      </p>
      <p>
       There is also the
       <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_national_baseball_team" title="Trinidad and Tobago national baseball team">
        Trinidad and Tobago national baseball team
       </a>
       which is controlled by the Baseball/Softball Association of Trinidad and Tobago, and represents the nation in international competitions. The team is a provisional member of the
       <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_Baseball_Confederation" title="Pan American Baseball Confederation">
        Pan American Baseball Confederation
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       There are a number of 9 and 18-hole
       <a href="/wiki/Golf" title="Golf">
        golf
       </a>
       courses on Trinidad and Tobago. The most established is the St Andrews Golf Club, Maraval in Trinidad (commonly referred to as Moka), and there is a newer course at Trincity, near Piarco Airport called Millennium Lakes. There are 18-hole courses at Chaguramas and Point-a-Pierre and 9-hole courses at Couva and St Madeline. Tobago has two 18-hole courses. The older of the two is at Mount Irvine, with the Magdalena Hotel &amp; Golf Club (formerly Tobago Plantations) being built more recently.
      </p>
      <p>
       Although a minor sport, bodybuilding is of growing interest in Trinidad and Tobago. Heavyweight female bodybuilder Kashma Maharaj is of Trinidadian descent.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="National_symbols">
        National symbols
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: National symbols">

        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">

        </a>

        </div>
       </div>
      </div>

        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">

          </a>
         </div>
         The coat of arms of Trinidad and Tobago
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:251px;">

        </a>

         </div>
         The Chaconia (
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Warszewiczia_coccinea" title="Warszewiczia coccinea">
           Warszewiczia coccinea
          </a>
         </i>
         ) is the national flower of Trinidad and Tobago.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Flag">
        Flag
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Flag">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Flag of Trinidad and Tobago">
        Flag of Trinidad and Tobago
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The flag was chosen by the Independence committee in 1962. Red, black and white symbolise the warmth of the people, the richness of the earth and water respectively.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gov_83-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-gov-83">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
        <a href="#cite_note-84">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Coat_of_arms">
        Coat of arms
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Coat of arms">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Coat of arms of Trinidad and Tobago">
        Coat of arms of Trinidad and Tobago
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The coat of arms was designed by the Independence committee, and features the
       <a href="/wiki/Scarlet_ibis" title="Scarlet ibis">
        scarlet ibis
       </a>
       (native to Trinidad), the
       <a href="/wiki/Rufous-vented_chachalaca" title="Rufous-vented chachalaca">
        cocrico
       </a>
       (native to Tobago) and hummingbird. The shield bears three ships, representing both the Trinity, and the three ships that Columbus sailed.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gov_83-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-gov-83">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Orders_and_decorations">
        Orders and decorations
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Orders and decorations">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       There are five categories and thirteen classes of national awards:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
        <a href="#cite_note-85">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Republic_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Order of the Republic of Trinidad and Tobago">
         Order of the Republic of Trinidad and Tobago
        </a>
        (formerly The
        <a href="/wiki/Trinity_Cross" title="Trinity Cross">
         Trinity Cross
        </a>
        Medal of the Order of the Trinity) in Gold only.
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Chaconia_Medal" title="Chaconia Medal">
         Chaconia Medal
        </a>
        , in Gold, Silver and Bronze.
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Hummingbird_Medal" title="Hummingbird Medal">
         Hummingbird Medal
        </a>
        , in Gold, Silver and Bronze.
       </li>
       <li>
        The Public Service Medal of Merit, in Gold, Silver and Bronze.
       </li>
       <li>
        The Medal for the Development of Women, in Gold, Silver and Bronze
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="National_songs">
        National songs
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: National songs">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The National Anthem of the twin-island state is "
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Forged_From_The_Love_of_Liberty" title="Forged From The Love of Liberty">
        Forged From The Love of Liberty
       </a>
       ".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
        <a href="#cite_note-86">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
        <a href="#cite_note-87">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Other national songs include "God Bless Our Nation"
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
        <a href="#cite_note-88">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and "Our Nation's Dawning".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
        <a href="#cite_note-89">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="National_birds">
        National birds
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: National birds">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The national birds for Trinidad and Tobago are the
       <a href="/wiki/Scarlet_ibis" title="Scarlet ibis">
        scarlet ibis
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Rufous-vented_chachalaca" title="Rufous-vented chachalaca">
        cocrico
       </a>
       . The scarlet ibis is kept safe by the government by living in the Caroni Bird Sanctuary which was set up by the government for the protection of these birds. The Cocrico is more indigenous to the island of Tobago and are more likely to be seen in the forest.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
        <a href="#cite_note-90">
         [90]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

         <th class="navbox-group" scope="row" style="width:1%">
          <a href="/wiki/Help:Authority_control" title="Help:Authority control">
           Authority control
          </a>
         </th>
         <td class="navbox-list navbox-odd" style="text-align:left;border-left-width:2px;border-left-style:solid;width:100%;padding:0px">
          <div style="padding:0em 0.25em">
           <ul>
            <li>
             <span class="nowrap">
              <a class="external text" href="https://www.worldcat.org/identities/containsVIAFID/122737458" rel="nofollow">
               WorldCat Identities
              </a>
             </span>
            </li>
            <li>
             <span class="nowrap">
              <a href="/wiki/Virtual_International_Authority_File" title="Virtual International Authority File">
               VIAF
              </a>
